< name>
Rustin Groody<//name>
< Text>
Matsuyama is a really unassuming place. It's quiet, and just enough out of the way that you might go by it without realizing. It's not big and fancy, sleek and stylish. It's quite homely, but also very cozy. But in a town that has several Japanese restaurants, Matsuyama has everything going for it.

The menu selection is pretty substantial, a great mix of classic items and their own creations. Their gyoza, in particular, are spot on. They have the special prices at lunchtime, which is a great reason for locals to visit during work, and the portions are always enough that you are getting two meals worth. Even when it comes to the sushi.

Now, one of my great shortcomings in life is that I can't eat sushi. But I can tell a story. I recently visited Matsuyama with a group of people who had never been there before, and many of whom enjoy sushi a lot. Every single one of them was impressed with the quantity and quality of sushi for the price.

Matsuyama's notoriety in town is firmly grounded in its delicious food. Which, you know...for a restaurant is probably a good thing. I say the next time you're feeling like treating yourself to something special, definitely give this a try.< /Text>

My husband and I have learned in our travels... that the best places to eat are not always the most popular. < Review>
I've been coming here for years (my parents live right down the street), and have always experienced high-quality food and service. About 10 years ago I hosted a dinner to celebrate my parents' 25-year anniversary. My last visit this May was no different. Unfailingly kind and professional staff. Delicious food: We had 3 appetizers, 5 entrees and 2 desserts, all wonderful. Notable is the fettuccine with filet tips and the venison special. My elderly mom's original pasta dish had too much garlic for her taste and the server graciously insisted on bringing another of the same dish. Then the chef came out to make sure it was to her liking. Very much appreciated. I've always loved the location and interior of this restaurant. Highly recommend!<//Review>

The menu changes daily and they always offer a variety that includes something for everyone. They are renowned for their pork chops, but the fish and beef prep is on par. This is my go to for special occasions and one of the best restaurants in the bay area.< /Review>< user>

<user>106139177309825733203< /user><Name>Ken Morrison< /Name>< Time>
1569250582548</Time>
<Rate>1< /Rate>< text>
Me, my wife and two close friends went to Cafe Sparrow for Sunday brunch after a round of golf.  We have eaten here several times for dinner and it's never disappointed us; until now.  We all ordered different dishes, and the other three ordered the bottomless mimosas and I had coffee.  Drinks came out immediately, but the food took just about an hour.  Not sure what happened, but nevertheless, when it arrived, it was one order short; mine.  This stuff  happens, I get it, but how professional this issue is handled, speaks to the establishments customer service, or the lack there of.  Our server said my order was coming, but didn't make it out for another 15-20 minutes.  Everyone around the table tried to wait, but when their food started to get cold, they ate.  After my food did arrive, the server said, "well, I guess maybe I never placed your order".  It's too bad that the poor service we received overshadowed how good my meal was.  Pretty disappointed brunch.</text>

<text>A special occasion made better

My wife and I returned to Cafe Sparrow in celebration of our wedding anniversary. It turned out to be a candlelight dinner via mother nature. The electrical power went out while we were enjoying out starters. The staff didn‚Äôt miss a beat, as extra candles were brought to the tables. The full house of patrons were at ease and all appeared to enjoy the experience.

This is probably our 6th visit to Cafe Sparrow in the past 4 years, and we have not been disappointed. I had the Chicken livers, which were prepared with apples, bacon, and garlic, without any of the condiments being overwhelming, and mixing nicely with the chicken liver. My wife had the special risotto with beef dish. We paired these with a Zinfandel from their wine list, and sat back and enjoyed a wonderful evening.
Even under the handicap of no power, the kitchen was able to provide their wonderful desserts.

This will be an evening that we will remember for quite some time.....</text>< Name>

50 minutes into the meal, became concerned about the entrees arrival. Expressed my concern to waitress, and I was told " oh, you should have told me you needed to leave so soon" (Evidently, I incorrectly thought that 1 hr and 15 minutes was enough time for a meal with a very early reservation and only 3 other tables seated!)

My immediate thought was "she forgot to put in our ticket, or the kitchen is backed up"

1 hr and 5 minutes after prompt arrival, still no entree, so, we had to leave because I was taking my 10 year daughter to a movie on our special night out. No way to enjoy entr√©e at this late juncture.

< review>
When I drove out to CA two years I was told that the air conditioner pulley was going bad... but it was not an immediate issue or anything to worry about.. would cost $400 to fix.. So I waited.

While getting an oil change here in CA I was told the same thing again.

I waited.

We take off yesterday and get down the hill, as we say, and all of a sudden I lost my power steering and the car is over heating, just before we reached the edge of Chico

The place that I had my oil changed was just up the road by about three blocks.

We have less then 30 min to get an appointment

We pull into Pro-Lube and the tech comes out and I tell him what happened and also say we have to get to an appointment..

He pops the hood and sure enough the pulley is gone and the serpentine belt is off of all the other pulleys that cool the engine and do what ever they are suppose to do...

He goes right to work.. In the mean time we call a taxi to pick us up.... the tech calls ORiely's orders the pulley, he meets the delivery girl in the parking lot puts the pulley on and the belt and has us done in 10 mins!!

Never have I seen a repair job go so fast...

He charges me the whole total of ...

$24.99 just the cost of the part!!!

As we are getting in the car the taxi pulls up and he goes over and takes care of that for us.

And we made it to the DR's office with 10 min. to spare!

And he told us as an extra bonus that whenever they do any service work they always include a free car wash. He says come back any time and he will remember us

Guess where we will always be getting our oil changed from now on??

It was a complete blessing from God that that was the perfect location for it to happen, that I actual knew where to go, that I had used them in the past and this tech was there...</review>

<text>Great service, great food.

The staff are friendly and prompt, with a pot of hot tea delivered almost as soon as you sit down, refilled before you can empty it. The staff seem genuinely happy and friendly. When you eat the food, you understand why- who wouldn't be happy to serve such wonderful food?

The food is absolutely delicious. The portions are generous and reasonably priced. The sign outside says "best dumplings and noodles in LA" and it just might be right. The dumplings are fresh, and I suspect they're hand-made in the restaurant- they've got that irregular look you don't find in the store-bought variety.

Eating at Mandarin Deli reminds me of when I was a child, 20+ years ago, and my Gung-Gung and Po-Po would take us out to eat at these wonderful Chinese restaurants in Hawaii and San Francisco. The atmosphere is calming, the food is fare worth getting emotional over, and the service is top-notch.</text>< user_name>
Kumar Corcoran<//user_name>

<rating>4<//rating><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Text>For all those who are hearing about Mandarin Deli restaurant for the first time, let me first say this: this restaurant is actually an authentic Chinese cuisine restaurant. Yes, one of the rare ones in LA country that serves authentic Mandarin China style food. It's nothing too spectacular, since it's sorta like villager style food, but it's a treat worth mentioning because it's really the only one in LA.

The specialty item here is the BEEF NOODLE SOUP. It's beef stew cooked in broth soy sauce soup with noodles (hand made or regular) and cilantros. Not too many Chinese restaurants serve this, so definitely try this one. It's pretty delicious and filling. The other notable dishes here are the scallion pancakes and pan fried dumplings.

I gave the restaurant a 4 instead of 5 because the Mandarin Deli location in Monterrey Park is a little better than this one in terms of taste. Chinese neighborhood, it's pretty understandable, eh? Anyways, even this Northridge location's food beats the hell out of the majority of Americanized, tasteless Chinese restaurants out in LA country right now.

So if you're in Northridge, and happen to see this place, give it a try. You won't be disappointed. And this is coming from a Chinese dude<//Text><name>Steve Cha<//name>< GmapID>

<Pics>None</Pics>< review>
This is an okay restaurant for some mandarin cuisine. I know some other great places with really good prices. But if you don't want to drive an extra 15 minutes, so be it. This place is an okay place for some potstickers and noodles. The main thing here is to eat is potstickers and beef stew noodle soup. Both which makes this place famous for. Other things that are served here are not that popular. This place hardly ever gets busy. Yet, I have been coming here since I was a kid. At the time, this place was the only place selling dumplings and noodles with beef stew in soup. Towards the late 90s, this place has grown, so has the furniture, the bathrooms, the ambience..it has grown very dull. The music that seldomly plays does put a nice touch when it DOES play. But other than that, it's really dead here. Same owner, same waitresses from when I was a child. The prices may have risen, but the food quality is not that great anymore. It's still a treat for those who live around the area and who don't have modes of transportation. You should come here. Like I said.. dumplings are a good treat. Just I have grown away from this place.<//review>

I also ate their sopa mixta, the conch meat soup with coconut milk, which was also very tasty, especially if you love seafood.
